Vyborg–Petrozavodsk Offensive	result	Strategic stalemateref|The Soviet offensive resulted in an advance of 100-130 kilometers, captured the city of Vyborg, and the Vyborg Bay islands. In doing this it removed the threat to Leningrad From the north and gave the Baltic Fleet much more freedom of action. However the offensive failed to drive Finland immediately out of the war, and from mid-July, Soviet forces started to redeploy to the Narva front in Estonia|group=\

The Hardest Day	result	Unsustainable attrition for both sidesref|The laurels for the day\u2019s action went to the defenders. The aim of the Luftwaffe was to wear down the Fighter Command without suffering excessive losses in the process, and in this it had failed. It cost the attackers five aircrew killed, wounded, or taken prisoner, for each British pilot casualty. In terms of aircraft, it had cost the Luftwaffe five bombers and fighters for every three Spitfires and Hurricanes destroyed in the air or on the ground. If the battle continued at this rate the Luftwaffe would wreck Fighter Command, but it would come close to wrecking itself in the process.|group=\
